  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_626842a8-9a04-4711-991b-fab52a730530'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

Damen’s only hope of reclaiming his throne is to fight together with Laurent against their usurpers.<br /> <br />Forced into an uneasy alliance the two princes journey deep into Akielos, where they face their most dangerous opposition yet. But even if the fragile trust they have built survives the revelation of Damen’s identity—can it stand against the Regent's final, deadly play for the throne?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7735171719049966824">I didn't think it possible, but Pacat has outdone herself. I literally finished this book 2 minutes ago and I'm breathless and flushed, and my heart pounds too fast. Don't expect a cool and collected review from me yet, for now I'll just go with: epic conclusion to a magnificent series.<br/><br/>Review probably to come. :')<br/><br/><br/><b>Update 9/7/15</b>: <br/><br/>Aaaaaand we have an anticipation increasing blurb!   <span id="freeText7735171719049966824" style="display:none">I didn't think it possible, but Pacat has outdone herself. I literally finished this book 2 minutes ago and I'm breathless and flushed, and my heart pounds too fast. Don't expect a cool and collected review from me yet, for now I'll just go with: epic conclusion to a magnificent series.<br><br>Review probably to come. :')<br><br><br><b>Update 9/7/15</b>: <br><br>Aaaaaand we have an anticipation increasing blurb! And according to Penguin CP 3 will be 384 pages.:D <br><br><b>Update 6/26/15</b>: <br><br>Official publication date for CP 3: 02-02-2016. <br><br>I'm a tad surprised and disappointed that it won't be out for the holidays, but shortly after. <br><br>Kings Rising snippet <a href="http://freece.livejournal.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. <br><br><b>Update 6/23/15</b>: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435048127i/15294557.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2 days now...<br><br><b> Update 1/24/15</b>: Not sure if everyone knows yet, but the title and cover for the third book (that 'leaked' earlier via an Australian ebook site) have been confirmed.;) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428663586i/14461337._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Source: Penguin Australia <br><br>Kings. I know! Rising. I can't even.<br><br><b> Update 1/24/15</b>: Penguin's version of CP 1 is released on 4/7/15. CP 2 will be released on 7/7/15. This is how they are different from the earlier released versions: CP 1 contains a bonus story. CP 2 contains a new chapter. <br><br>Are the extras worth buying the new versions? What do you guys think?!<br><br>PS how much prettier is the Australian cover of CP 2 compared to the US cover? Gah.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428480152i/14431128._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428480353i/14431153.jpg" width="250" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b> Update 1/24/15</b>: So! This is really intriguing, y'all. A friend (thanks Eva!) linked me to an Australian ebook site that had already published the expected publication date (10/28/15) and the title for book 3 on its website: KINGS RISING. Only hours later, the information was deleted again... <br><br>Mysterious, no? <br><br>Kings Rising....what do we think? Sounds like a legitimate (and oh so exciting) title?<br><br><b> Update 11/4/14</b>: Book 2 will be re-released in July 2015. So this could mean that book 3 may be released just before Christmas 2015. Think about it, it'd only make sense from a marketing perspective.:0) <br><br><b> Update 9/10/14</b>: A reassuring update from the author on her <a href="http://freece.livejournal.com/66809.html" rel="nofollow noopener">website</a>: She's still working on the manuscript for book 3, but promises that the 3 books will not be spaced anything like a year apart (see comments for my and friends' theories about the possible release dates).<br><br><b> Update 9/2/14</b>: We have an expected publication date for the first CP book (re-release): April 7th 2015. I know, with the current pacing we'll be gray and in wheelchairs by the time CP 3 finally sees the light of day.;p<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1407108920l/22571663.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Update 5/5/14</b>: The promised snippet from book 3 can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/6219111-gift-4---captive-prince---book-3-chapter-9---snippet?utm_medium=email&amp;utm_source=author_blog_post_digest" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>. Woop Woop!<br><br><b>Update 4/8/14</b>: Thanks to everyone who voted, Captive Prince won the DABWAHA tournament! Woot! C.S. Pacat's bribes include; a sneak-peak snippet from book 3, a DVD commentary for the sex scene in book 2 (complete with sexual position analysis), a manuscript-writing livestream where fans can chat and comment, an unofficial book 3 cover based on the original covers (pre-Penguin).<br><br><b>Update 12/15/13</b>: Did you guys all catch that, thanks to Rachel, there's a great <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/109088-captivated" rel="nofollow noopener">Captive Prince group</a> on Goodreads to discuss and fangirl/boy?<br><br><b>Update 12/7/13</b>: S.U. Pacat has changed her name into C.S. Pacat because "I made this change in conversation with various Penguins: we all thought it was better that I take this opportunity to choose a more serious author name that could have longevity across my writing career." (well, thank god for that! That 'funny' pen name was unworthy of the quality of her work). Other than that, no release date for book 3, but she's writing it faster than she had expected. So that's good. Full blog post <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5318627-c-s-pacat-name-change-announcement" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. <br><br><b>Update 9/25/13</b>: S.U. Pacat just posted a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/4920559-captive-prince-news-and-mini-faq" rel="nofollow noopener">blog post</a> with the latest news. Still no publication date for book 3, Penguin will not demand that Laurent is turned into Laurentia (thank god, LOL), there will be new covers (please no nekkid torsos!) <br>---------------------------------<br><i>Captive Prince</i> has been acquired by one of the largest publishers in the world: Penguin. Can you freaking believe it? Penguin has bought the entire trilogy and is going to release it in bookshops worldwide. <br><br>Such marvelous, exciting news for the author and for all of us m/m addicts! This could be a milestone when it comes to more recognition for the genre (more on the author's blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://freece.livejournal.com/61483.html">http://freece.livejournal.com/61483.html</a>). <br><br>Fantastic.:)<br><br>I'm not a fan of reviews with tons of giant gifs of crazy, excited people in it. But if I was I would have pasted every single one of them into this review. The anticipation is simply killing me! :D<br><br>I think I've found <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nlCPOCwo3FY" rel="nofollow noopener">my soundtrack</a> to these books.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1765293214377236490">OM G YM God <br/><br/>ok this is fine I'M FINE EVEYRTHIN GIT S FNIE <br/><br/>at first i was like o shit this probably isn't going to be gr8 but it was so gr8 i feel so gr8 after finishing this.<br/>This was so touching yet interesting and the characters were just so well-built and intricate even though I could predict some of the backstory that went behind their angstiness. <br/><br/>I remember reading this book and thinking "I only have one issue with it" but now that I'm done with the book and i'm typing this I literally don't</span>
  <span id="freeText1765293214377236490" style="display:none">OM G YM God <br /><br />ok this is fine I'M FINE EVEYRTHIN GIT S FNIE <br /><br />at first i was like o shit this probably isn't going to be gr8 but it was so gr8 i feel so gr8 after finishing this.<br />This was so touching yet interesting and the characters were just so well-built and intricate even though I could predict some of the backstory that went behind their angstiness. <br /><br />I remember reading this book and thinking "I only have one issue with it" but now that I'm done with the book and i'm typing this I literally don't remember what that was. The betrayals in this stung just as much as they were supposed to, it was gripping, the plot twists got me some whiplash, the climax was everything. I just think there was a lot of room for an epilogue and I heard rumors about there being an epilogue floating around somewhere and I would love to read it because it leaves off in a place where you're like [king george voice] what comes next <br /><br />definitely would highly recommend this series, even though the first one is sort of shameful. it's the only book that goes so far into rape and abuse and sexual assault, so if you can get through it, the rest of the series is full of amazing character development and war aspects and I JUST LOVE DAMEN AND LAURENT OK</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2047883094" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047883094" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047883094?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425273999" href="/book/show/25810368-kings-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047883094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3668245742291290558"><i>”To gain everything and lose everything in the space of a moment. That is the fate of all princes destined for the throne.”</i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>I. N. T. E. N. S. E.!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/>If I had to describe <b>“King’s Rising”</b> with one word it most certainly would be this one! This book was so damn freaking intense the tension was physically palpable in the air. It dripped from every single page, it consumed me, made me feel uncomfortable, giddy and so excited I could barely keep it in. <br/>Gosh this was actually so damn intense it will t</span>
  <span id="freeText3668245742291290558" style="display:none"><i>”To gain everything and lose everything in the space of a moment. That is the fate of all princes destined for the throne.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>I. N. T. E. N. S. E.!!!</u>
</b><br /><br />If I had to describe <b>“King’s Rising”</b> with one word it most certainly would be this one! This book was so damn freaking intense the tension was physically palpable in the air. It dripped from every single page, it consumed me, made me feel uncomfortable, giddy and so excited I could barely keep it in. <br />Gosh this was actually so damn intense it will take me ages to recover from that final book!!!<br /><br />As it seems Pacat isn’t only a master at manipulation but also of building up almost unbearable tension between her protagonists and boy did I live for it!!! &lt;333 <br />I loved this so much my heart overflowed with joy!!! XD<br /><b>This book is perfection!!!</b><br />It really is! <br /><br />The plot was so elaborate and ingenious that it was a pleasure to watch it unfold. Every little moment in this series had a purpose, a reason to exist and in <b>“King’s Rising”</b> we finally get to the core. Layer by layer we unravel the true scope of the Regent’s plans and Laurent’s ceaseless attempts to stifle the countless fires. Gosh, there were so many infinitesimal moments that added up to the entire story in the end, it was just brilliant and so very delightful to read! <br />(Boy, am I a happy camper or what? *LOL*) <br /><br />And don’t even get me started on the scenes between Laurent and Damen!!! <br /><b>
  <u>SO FREAKING INTENSE!!!</u>
</b><br />Wait, how often did I already use that word by now?! 4 times?! Yep, I think that’s enough for an introduction! XD Before I’m tempted to use it a fifth time we better head to the main part, the actual review! ;-)<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br /><br /><i>”The ache of loss didn’t make sense, because Laurent had never been his. He had known that. The delicate thing that had grown between them had never had a right to exist.”</i><br /><br />After the revelation of Damen’s true identity at the end of “Prince’s Gambit” Laurent and Damen don’t only have to face each other as King and Prince, but are also forced to deal with their new situation. If they truly want to depose the Regent and Kastor there is no other way than to trust each other, combine their forces and to become allies though. A task that most certainly won’t be as simple as it sounds. Their enemies are closing in, their armies clash, the fate of two kingdoms is at stake and between all that their hearts continue to burn with the heat of uncontrollable desire. <br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Fair warning! This is the part where I usually quote the hell out of the book and go into detail about the plot and the main characters. So yeah, there will be a lot of spoilers in your near future and if you don’t want to be spoiled I advise you to leave now! ;-)</u>
</b> <br /><br /><b>Damen – The King</b><br /><br /><i>”For the first time, he caught a glimmer of what Laurent would be like as a king. He saw him, not as the Regent’s unready nephew, not as Auguste’s younger brother, but as himself, a young man with a collection of talents thrown into leadership too early, and taking it on, because he was given no other choice. I would serve him, he thought, and that itself was like a revelation.”</i><br /><br />It was so wonderful to watch how easily he slipped into the role of a king! I mean I always knew that Damen would make a great king but to actually see it and to experience how he took his rightful place was something entirely different! The dynamics between him and Laurent were really interesting to watch because for once he actually had the upper hand. Not when it came to scheming, mind you, *lol* but when it came to the strength and sheer force of his army he definitely trumped him. XD I loved that he didn’t let his experiences get him down, he still fought and he didn’t hide his scars. No, he accepted them as a part of him and as a part of his own history and in the end this made him an even better king. Still, I always felt sorry for Damen when he fell into old habits or when he encountered other slaves. &gt;_&lt; I just hope that he’ll be able to heal his wounds in “The Summer Palace”. =))<br /><br /><i>”He felt the limits of his own nature, which too easily swung to anger, and the need – stymied by circumstance – to bring about the Regent’s death. All he wanted was to take up his sword and cut a path into Ios.”</i><br /><br /><i>”There was a man I was supposed to meet. He’s got all these ideas about honour and fair play, and he tries to keep me from doing the wrong thing. But he’s not here right now. Unfortunately for you.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I thought I’d let you go up and down a few times,” said Damen, “before I take you.”<br />“I thought you were down here because you couldn’t take me.”</i><br /><br /><i>”That is the man you face. He has more honour and integrity than any man I have ever met. He is dedicated to his people and his country. And I am proud to have been his lover.” <br />Damen said it with his eyes on Laurent, willing him to know how much he meant it, and for a moment Laurent just gazed back at him, his eyes blue and wide.</i><br /><br /><b>Laurent – The Prince</b><br /><br /><i>”A ludicrous boyish hope flared that someone would come to help him, and, carefully, he extinguished it. Since the age of thirteen, there had been no rescuer, for his brother was dead.”</i><br /><br />I loved that we got Laurent’s POV!!! Admittedly it was just for a chapter but this chapter was amazing!!! To finally be able to see how he thinks!!! To be in his head without all those barriers he built to protect himself! After all this time we finally saw the true Laurent and damn it, but he’s such a broken boy. T_T And yet despite all that, despite every experience he made, he still decided to trust Damen, he opened up to him and eventually fell in love with the man who killed his brother. <b>Oh my, what a poor, lonely, tortured and conflicted soul!!!</b> &lt;333 I could understand his hatred for Damen, especially because he always knew who he was and I guess to see that he wasn’t the monster he believed him to be must have been extremely painful. He lost his brother and then he found him in Damen again… &gt;_&lt; ARGH! I just wanted to hug him and tell him that everything is going to be alright. XD<br /><br /><i>”Laurent had always been capable of a kind of ruthless pragmatism. He was able to put emotion aside and do what he had to do to win, with a perfect and nauseating ability to ignore all human feeling.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Laurent had never needed to use force to make men obey him, just as he had never needed men to like him in order to get his way. Laurent got his way because when men tried to resist him, they found, sweetly outmanoeuvred, that they couldn’t.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Am I talking too much? I can’t hold alcohol at all.” <br />“I can see that.”<br />“It’s my fault. I never drink. I should have realised I’d need to, with men like these, and made an effort to … build up some sort of tolerance…” He was serious.</i><br /><br /><i>”A fair fight?” said Laurent, turning back to him, “No fight’s ever fair. Someone’s always stronger.”</i><br /><br /><b>Nikandros – The loyal friend</b><br /><br /><i>”And if I call on you to fight?”<br />“Then we fight,” said Nikandros. “Together.”<br />The straightforward ease of it left him without words. He had forgotten what home felt like. He had forgotten trust, loyalty, kinship. Friends.</i><br /><br />I adore Nikandros! He’s such an amazing and loyal friend and I loved how much he cared about Damen’s well-being. Not because he was his king but because he actually truly cared about him. Poor Damen though, he had to fight a lot for his relationship with Laurent, considering what he did to him I can’t blame Nikandros for disapproving of their love though. The moment in the tent after the fight with Pallas was one of the most intense scenes in the entire book and I really, really like Nikandros!!! XD<br /><br /><b>Jokaste – The true cast-iron bitch:</b><br /><br /><i>”You weren’t expecting what it felt like when he touched you. You weren’t expecting the weight of his body, how it felt to have his attention, to have him want you.”<br />“You left out the part near the end, when it was so good I let myself forget what he’d done.”<br />“Oh dear,” said Jokaste. “That was the truth.”</i><br /><br />That evil bitch!!! I hated her so much and yet I could understand her! <b>URGH!</b> In a sick and twisted way she truly loved Damen and only sold him into slavery in order to save his life. Still, the wounds she inflicted run deep and I’ll never like her because of that. Yes, she saved his life, but she also almost killed him with it. The conversation between her and Laurent was one of the best highlights of the series though and it would be a lie to claim I didn’t enjoy every delicious and juicy moment of it!!! No, actually I loved it!! *lol* &lt;333 <b>
  <u>So much hatred and tension!</u>
</b> Ahh it was such a delight to read! XD My cunning and crafty faerie heart couldn’t help but relish their encounter with enthusiastic joy! ;-P I just live for moments like this! Haha! &lt;3<br /><br /><b>Dament – Their relationship</b><br /><br /><i>”I hated you,” said Laurent. “I hated you so badly I thought I’d choke on it. If my uncle hadn’t stopped me, I would have killed you. And then you saved my life, and every time I needed you, you were there, and I hated you for that, too.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>TENSION!!!</u>
</b> So much tension it almost killed me while I read the book!! Their relationship was so complicated and rough in “King’s Rising”!!! Now that they both met each other as king and prince they had to live up to certain expectations and they tried everything possible to follow the rules. Of course the heart and the mind are always two different things and I think you could see that inner conflict on every page of the book. Still, I loved their honesty and their strength, that they both didn’t yield and that they tried to make it work somehow. XD It was a long way until they reached that moment though and as usual Pacat taunted us with the promise of a wonderful relationship in the future. *lol*<br /><br />*sigh* There were so many awesome scenes in that book and I can’t mention them all, but there definitely were some moments I’ll never forget! For instance their fight in the training area! It was so freaking amazing and it was such a good picture of their relationship! The way Laurent tried to defend himself with everything he had and the realisation that he just couldn’t win against Damen. He didn’t only win their fight but also Laurent’s heart! Pacat! Well done!!! This was such a brilliant way to describe their relationship I have to pay you my respect! XD <br /><br /><b>AND</b> speaking of amazing scenes!!! Can we take a look at the chapter in which they appear united for the very first time?! OMG!!! Laurent’s gift to Damen! The whipping of the clan mercenaries! Gosh!! That was such a mean and deliberate move! XD Damen’s retort however wasn’t less sophisticated though. *lol* To gift him with his golden slave cuff!!! <b>Good lord!!!</b> ARGH I LOVE THOSE TWO BOYS SO MUCH!!! *LOL* &lt;3333<br /><br />They certainly didn’t make it easy for each other and their heated word duels always had me at the edge of my seat! XD What I also loved was the fact that they both always seemed to know what the other one needed. Whenever one of them was about to lose control, they both didn’t even hesitate and were there to catch each other if need be. This was so damn beautiful!!! My heart just ached for them!! &lt;333 <br /><br />BUT the last couple of chapters! That moment when Laurent actually begged his uncle for Damen’s life!!! <b>
  <u>OH. MY. GOD.!!!!</u>
</b> Laurent my precious, beautiful and hurt boy knelt in front of his uncle to save Damen’s life!!! The man who killed his brother, the man he trusted more than anyone else, the man he loved more than his own life!!! <b>ARGH!!! MY HEART!!! YOU ARE NOT ALONE LAURENT!!!! YOU ARE LOVED!!!! GOSH, I CAN’T EVEN…. &lt;333</b><br />I’m dead!!! T_T<br /><br /><i>”Shall I ask you how you did it? What he looked like when your sword went in?”<br />“No,” said Damen.<br />“Or shall I tell you about the illusion of the man who gave me good counsel. Who stood by me. Who never lied to me.”<br />“I never lied to you.”<br />The words were awful in the silence that followed them.</i><br /><br /><i>”I miss you,” said Laurent. “I miss our conversations.”</i><br /><br /><i>”How can you trust me, after what your own brother did to you?”<br />“Becaues he was false,” said Damen, “and you are true. I have never known a truer man.” He said, into the stillness, “I think if I gave you my heart, you would treat it tenderly.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I killed your brother.”<br />“I know.”<br />Damen said it, and felt a strange empathy pass between them, as if they knew each other for the first time.</i><br /><br /><i>”Now, Laurent was beside him. Aloof, untouchable Laurent was beside him, kneeling on the wet marble hundreds of miles from home, with nothing in his eyes but Damen.”</i><br /><br /><i>Laurent was very still, and the moment seemed to draw out, the space between them private in the hushed baths. <br />”And the centre. We both hold the centre,” said Laurent. And then: “It was one kingdom, once.”</i><br /><br /><b>The conclusion:</b><br /><br />I loved “King’s Rising” even more than I loved “Prince’s Gambit” and this series definitely is one of my all-time favourites now! =)) <br />Since this was another buddy read my special thanks go to my adorable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66222749-lia-bonnibel-hiatus" rel="nofollow noopener">Gansey</a>!! Girl, thank you so much for reading this book with me! I loved our conversations and that we just couldn’t seem to be able to stop gushing about Laurent and Damen! &lt;333 It was so much fun to experience this series with you and I’m so damn thankful I got to know you through goodreads!!! Let’s buddy read even more series together! I’m so ready! XD &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="3668245742291290558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_689239897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689239897" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689239897?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25792894-kings-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689239897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9147347302227960007">Like earlier books in this series, 'Kings Rising' had my rapt attention from beginning to end. This book was action-packed and full of emotion. It broke my heart, only to piece it back together slowly. I loved every minute!<br/><br/>This book sees both Damen and Laurent fighting to reclaim their kingdoms. Despite their differences, the two are forced into a tenuous alliance. They need one another, if either of them hopes to succeed. This makes for plenty of emotional highs and lows along the way as the tw</span>
  <span id="freeText9147347302227960007" style="display:none">Like earlier books in this series, 'Kings Rising' had my rapt attention from beginning to end. This book was action-packed and full of emotion. It broke my heart, only to piece it back together slowly. I loved every minute!<br /><br />This book sees both Damen and Laurent fighting to reclaim their kingdoms. Despite their differences, the two are forced into a tenuous alliance. They need one another, if either of them hopes to succeed. This makes for plenty of emotional highs and lows along the way as the two attempt to navigate through their new realities. In many ways, the tables have turned. At the same time, so much remains unchanged.<br /><br />Finally, all of Damen's secrets are out in the open. No longer does he live in fear of what will happen when Laurent finds out who he really is. Instead, he now lives with his wrath. If he thought that Laurent would be angry, he was right.<br /><br />To say that I found this a little hypocritical is putting it mildly. I kept thinking, "where does Laurent get off?" After all, Damen was his slave by force. Of course he would keep a secret like that. What did he expect him to do, tell his captor his true identity and face certain death? <br /><br />That feeling only grew stronger as Laurent revealed some secrets of his own. I mean, where did he get off being so self-righteous? It seemed to me that Damen was played, yet again. If anything, Laurent proved, once again, to be one of the most manipulative characters that I've ever encountered.<br /><br />Even so, I cannot deny that I absolutely loved this book. Every interaction between Damen and Laurent was like a delicious little drop of heaven for me. I spent the moments between their encounters holding my breath, waiting for their next interaction. It was pathetic really, but I have no shame.<br /><br />In the end, I was left feeling quite satisfied. I wasn't sure that these two would ever get there, but they eventually get some peace. I'm not a big fan of M/M romances generally, but I absolutely loved this series. It was heartfelt and sexy, with plenty of action along the way. The characters and storyline were well-developed and engaging. I would definitely recommend this series to others.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookadddicthaven.com">www.bookadddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9147347302227960007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1535706426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535706426" />
    <a title="Jackeli08" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14553257-jackeli08"><img alt="Jackeli08" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1535706426?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackeli08" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackeli08" href="/user/show/14553257-jackeli08">Jackeli08</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1535706426&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535706426" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16899260501920334807">Dear Author,<br/>First of all I would like to compliment you on book 1 and 2 of this saga, because they not only were written exceptionally well, they also bespoke of an acute, detail/oriented, forward/thinking mind. Unfortunately, these are also the reasons behind my poor rating: while your writing ability remains intact, the carefully planned strategies you had shown us in the past two books quite simply disappear, and are replaced by sheer luck. <br/>SPOILERS AHEAD<br/>Chapter two: Laurent wakes up bound to</span>
  <span id="freeText16899260501920334807" style="display:none">Dear Author,<br />First of all I would like to compliment you on book 1 and 2 of this saga, because they not only were written exceptionally well, they also bespoke of an acute, detail/oriented, forward/thinking mind. Unfortunately, these are also the reasons behind my poor rating: while your writing ability remains intact, the carefully planned strategies you had shown us in the past two books quite simply disappear, and are replaced by sheer luck. <br />SPOILERS AHEAD<br />Chapter two: Laurent wakes up bound to a chair in the prison cells of Fontaine and the only thing we are told is that there was an ambush and that Laurent does not want to think about what happened to his men. How is this possible Miss Pacat? We leave Laurent at the end of book two with 120 riders that have just demonstrated their worth at Hellay and are ready to fight to take Fortaine, to suddenly find out, without any explanation, that said strong contingent has not only been ambushed and defeated (how? by a stronger contingent? If so, whose men where those?), but that Laurent, when he saw his men being attacked and understood he might loose, did not even try to send a messenger to Damen to inform him. But let us suspend our judgment for a minute and concentrate on Laurent, bound to that chair, with his right shoulder dislocated and with the hilt of a knife protruding from it: ladies and gentlemen, prepare yourselves for a miracle: Laurent manages to pick up a heavy oak chair and swing it with enough force to stun and later kill Govert. Now, I am not a medical doctor, but this whole scene seems a bit far fetched to me, and more appropriate to a Rambo/like film. Miss Pacat however has not finished: Laurent is now free, while Guion is confined inside the cell, and the author presents the situation as if it were Laurent the one with the upper hand. But let us reflect one minute: we were told that the Prince of Vere was tied to a chair in the cells of Fortaine, which means that he actually was inside Fortaine, which means that, even if he managed to escape his cell he still is inside the enemy’s fortress, and I do not suppose that an enemy fortress is quite that easy to escape from. Moreover Laurent’s threat to leave Guion inside the cell is supposedly enough to convince him to cooperate, but there are two main problems with this scenario: if the master of the keep suddenly disappears I do believe that his people would search for him, and they would presumably search the whole keep, and the cells are part of it, so it would be quite impossible not to find him. Secondly, let us imagine we are Guion: Laurent threatens us and we are scared enough to accept his conditions... But as soon as Laurent let us out from that cell our best interest would be to renege our deal and to kill him: he is alone in our keep, where the men are loyal to us and his uncle would reward us for it, while helping Laurent would only cause us problems, so Guion’s sudden choice to help the Prince of Vere does not truly make sense. <br />Chapter three: who are the prince’s men camped outside Fortaine? Are they what remains of Laurent’s forces after they were ambushed? Are they Fortaine keep’s men that became the prince’s men when Guion shifted his loyalties? Or are they part of the Regent’s army, sent to help Guion ambush Laurent’s forces? And, if so, why has their commander suddenly decided to abandon the Regent? Just because Guion said so? <br />Chapter four: Laurent bargains with Damen. This is where Laurent’s personality goes from rational and calculating to emotional: the prince needs Damen’s help to win the war, and he decides the best way to do that is to reveal to his would be ally how he used and manipulated him, and then to threaten him. The author would have us believe that a man like Laurent, instead of using Damen’s feelings to further his own goals, decides to unload his resentment and bitterness right when a united front would be most important. <br />Chapter seven: the banner men of Delpha are called to pledge themselves to fight alongside Damen, and one of them is worried that Vere could have undue influence over Akieos due to the fact that Laurent and Damen are lovers. Laurent is able to assuage Barieus’ fears telling him that one would be ice/cold to sleep with one’s brother’s killer, so basically denying the accusation. A few chapters later however Laurent and Damen are discovered by an akielon soldier while in bed together, and inexplicably nobody is surprised or angered by this, especially the Veretians show no reaction to the fact that their leader is bedding the prince/killer, alias who is probably the most hated man in the whole country. Nobody questions Laurent’s decision or leadership, nobody worries about Damen’s possible influence over him. <br />Chapter nine: the games. Miss Pacat, I do understand the need to make the lead character stronger and better than everybody else, but there is no need to make him super/human. Not only in chapter two Damen, like a perfect killing machine, seems almost able to win the fight all by himself, but now he is even able to catch a flying spear with his bare hand, and than, not satisfied enough with that, he is able to throw it ”over the full, impossible length of the field, to thunk into the target alongside Laurent’s spear...”. Bravo Terminator!<br />Let us talk about Makedon now: there are no shadows of gray with his character, in fact at first he hates all things Veretian, and then, after Laurent’s skill at okton and at drinking he does a 180 turn and suddenly he behaves warmly towards the prince and speaks to him ”as he might with a favoured nephew a bit slow at learning”. This seems a bit far fetched to me and not an appropriate reflection of reality, exactly like a teetotaler suddenly able not only to drink a lot, but to maintain control and best an usual drinker to a game. <br />Furthermore, during the discussion about tactics Laurent is completely silent... What a change from the prince we met in the second book, that stayed awake long hours at night to discuss precisely tactics with Damen.!<br />Chapter thirteen: after their night together Damen and Laurent talk together and Laurent describes his plans and contingencies, and this makes Damen quite happen because he sees it as a way for the prince to be open with him. But at kingsmeet, later on, we discover that Laurent had decided from the beginning to give himself up to his uncle in exchange for the child, so when Laurent spoke with Damen either he lied to him or omitted the truth. In any case this shows a lack of trust between the two and results in a situation in which Laurent (the supposed strategist), is completely at the mercy of his uncle and it befalls Damen to think of a way to free him.<br />Chapter seventeen to the end: here lies my main problem with the book, in fact what happens in these three chapters is pure, unaltered, sheer luck and not the forward thinking, the complicated strategies, Miss Pacat has enthralled us with in the previous books. First problem: Damien decides to come alone to Ios and to surrender himself to the regent. This leads to his being brought in front of the Veretian council, where Laurent is being tried: Damen is lucky, because nothing guaranteed this particular outcome, which in fact clearly benefits only him, and neither his half/brother or the regent (usually quite smart), that could have, for example kept him in a cell to deal with later, at their own convenience. In chapter eighteen we discover Damen great plan is to call Guion to the stand, which results in utter disaster, until we find out that Laurent’s plan had been all along to have Guion’s wife testify: so now the author suggests that Laurent planned this whole situation, presumably to save the day, but only a few pages later we find out that Laurent brought Loyse simply to clear Damen’s name. How in the world does this make sense? Laurent's great plan would be this: in case Damen is as stupid as me, and decides to simply give himself up, like a sacrificial lamb, I will make sure to bring a witness to testify his innocence, except that this will not help him at all, because the minute Damen gives himself up to the regent and to Kastor he is dead, regardless of the council’s decision, and I refuse to believe that a mind like Laurent did not understand this. The only possible explanation is that Laurent has transformed into a besotted fool, which is truly a shame, because in this case means that love, instead of making him stronger, has simply reduced his intellectual faculties. But now comes the best part: Damen, the loyal brute we all know and love, has a moment of brilliance and makes a connection nobody, not even Laurent (our resident genius) had been able to do before: there is somebody in that group able to testify against the regent: again sheer luck. But this is not simply luck, this is the ”Deus ex/machina” one would expect from a playwrighter, something spectacular and unexpected, able to solve any problem and guarantee an total victory for our heroes, without any planning needed. There is only one problem with this kind of device: you need to suspend belief, you need not question how it happened, because soon as you do that, you realize it is completely unbelievable. Does the author truly want us to believe that miraculously Damen made that connection and that the man with all the answers is right there, ready to speak and with a very convenient letter that he brought with him, just in case something like this were to happen? And why has this man not spoken before (for example with Laurent)? And if Damen had not called him out, would he not have spoken on his own? And how many probabilities were there that this mysterious man, of all the people it could be (Jord, for example), is precisely the doctor, the right man in the right place? Again I repeat: sheer luck.<br />Finally, one last inaccuracy: Laurent has been bound with his hands behind his back for hours and hours, but a few minutes after being freed he is able to fight with a sword and to defeat a seasoned fighter like Kastor.<br /><br />Dear author, I am truly sorry, because you are a gifted writer and I cannot but ask myself how and why this whole débacle happened. As I do not personally know you (a shame because I would like to compliment you on the idea behind this saga and on the first two books, that were absolutely exceptional and breath/taking), the only thing I can say that changed between the first two books and the third is the publisher, Penguin, and I wonder if, and how, this might have had an impact on your work. <br />I wish you the best and hope you will continue your writing career, because a talent like yours rarely present itself. Please forgive me if my review was in any way offensive to you, I assure you this was not the intention but unfortunately when one has to criticize something the line between constructive critique and attack are not always that clear.<br /><br />Elena Giacon<br /><br />P.S. I beg your pardon for any grammatical mistakes, as an Italian I do often have troubles with English grammar...</span>
  <a data-text-id="16899260501920334807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1539282015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1539282015" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1539282015?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=all-the-feels">all-the-feels</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539282015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6264820277642562473"><br/>No rating. For now. Up until the 80% mark this was five stars all the way. But that ending...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418715886ra/12881963.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I feel like I should add more here, so I will. If I were forced to rate this now, based on the series as a whole, this would be a solid four stars. I guess what I'm saying is don't let this review concern you or keep you from reading these books. This ending is perfectly satisfactory. For <i>most</i> books. But after the level of brilliance in the second one in this series, it just can't compare. It was too nea</span>
  <span id="freeText6264820277642562473" style="display:none"><br>No rating. For now. Up until the 80% mark this was five stars all the way. But that ending...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418715886ra/12881963.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I feel like I should add more here, so I will. If I were forced to rate this now, based on the series as a whole, this would be a solid four stars. I guess what I'm saying is don't let this review concern you or keep you from reading these books. This ending is perfectly satisfactory. For <i>most</i> books. But after the level of brilliance in the second one in this series, it just can't compare. It was too neat. Too tidy. Too...<i>bloodless</i>. And that's why I'm having trouble rating it. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6264820277642562473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1260641157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260641157" />
    <a title="wesley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36179338-wesley"><img alt="wesley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446832327p2/36179338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260641157?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="wesley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="wesley" href="/user/show/36179338-wesley">wesley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=well-written">well-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=effeminate-characters">effeminate-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260641157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1699291551752221831">
  <i>Disclaimer: This is a combined review of all three books because I had to read everything in one go; else, I wouldn’t survive.</i>
<p>My first thought after I slightly recovered (heavy emphasis on ‘slightly’) from the Captive Prince magic was, <b>“This deserves a movie series!”</b></p><p>And, <b>“Why isn’t there a movie series yet?”</b></p><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455570474i/18120439._SY540_.jpg' width='400' alt='damen and laurent' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <i>Deviantart by: <a href='http://chiihun.deviantart.com/art/CaptivePrince-SUPacat-Novel-took-forever-384768526' rel='nofollow noopener'>chiihun</a></i>
</blockquote><p>Because no series is this vividly detailed yet deceptively good. From the onset, Pacat had created this intricate web – so perfectly woven and exquisitely </p></span>
  <span id="freeText1699291551752221831" style="display:none">
  <i>Disclaimer: This is a combined review of all three books because I had to read everything in one go; else, I wouldn’t survive.</i>
<p>My first thought after I slightly recovered (heavy emphasis on ‘slightly’) from the Captive Prince magic was, <b>“This deserves a movie series!”</b></p><p>And, <b>“Why isn’t there a movie series yet?”</b></p><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455570474i/18120439._SY540_.jpg" width="400" alt="damen and laurent" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>Deviantart by: <a href="http://chiihun.deviantart.com/art/CaptivePrince-SUPacat-Novel-took-forever-384768526" rel="nofollow noopener">chiihun</a></i>
</blockquote><p>Because no series is this vividly detailed yet deceptively good. From the onset, Pacat had created this intricate web – so perfectly woven and exquisitely crafted that you just can’t help but admire it, touch it and before you know it, you’ve been spun in her web, entangling you in silken beauty.</p><p>Pacat is a master story teller. Every word, phrase, sentence is purposeful and relevant. Every metaphor, symbolism, and foreshadowing amplified yet subdued. Pacat reinvents the rules of storytelling. Her brand is hers and hers alone.</p><p>I love every character she has introduced in each book. Each one, distinct and memorable. In each book, Pacat brought forth new flavors to old and new characters alike. No character stayed dormant with each one continuously evolving and growing along with the story. </p><p>Damen and Laurent’s relationship arc was perfectly crafted. In the first half of the series, I was unsure of the romance, because nothing is absolute with Pacat. But I admire how she cultivated their romance such that it stayed more as an undercurrent rather than a raging torrent. When the dam finally broke, all the push and pull of anticipation had been worth it. Straightforward, honest Damen and cold, cunning Laurent – the perfect opposition; Fire and Ice. Until the end, the tension between the two never wavered. These characters alone have added an extra layer to an already gripping and intriguing storyline.</p><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455570686i/18120469._SX540_.png" width="400" alt="laurent and damen collage" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><p>Reading this series can be likened to watching an exclusive game of chess. Every move is well thought of, every twist a revelation. It’s a steadily building series where strategy is key and can either end with a king’s checkmate or both kings on a stalemate. But you have to reach the end to find out. <i>*wink*</i></p> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1699291551752221831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539568154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3828639269104899217">► <b>No rating so far, possibly <i>forever</i></b>. I AM TOO CONFUSED.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454817027i/18017426.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Involvement</u>
</b> : I just binge read the three books in two days. I'm pretty sure that it speaks for itself. If not, <i>DUH</i>, these books are more addictive than Nutella. <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Exhilaration</u>
</b> : You can't even imagine how deep I fell for Laurent. Give me a tortured, complex end borderline psycho heart, I'll be intrigued. Add a twisted and convoluted mind, I'll lose my breathe. Make him genuinely smile and I'll love him forever. God, how he made me la</span>
  <span id="freeText3828639269104899217" style="display:none">► <b>No rating so far, possibly <i>forever</i></b>. I AM TOO CONFUSED.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454817027i/18017426.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Involvement</u>
</b> : I just binge read the three books in two days. I'm pretty sure that it speaks for itself. If not, <i>DUH</i>, these books are more addictive than Nutella. <br><br><b>
  <u>Exhilaration</u>
</b> : You can't even imagine how deep I fell for Laurent. Give me a tortured, complex end borderline psycho heart, I'll be intrigued. Add a twisted and convoluted mind, I'll lose my breathe. Make him genuinely smile and I'll love him forever. God, how he made me laugh. I adore him and <b>I MISS HIM ALREADY</b>.<br><br><b>
  <u>Mirth</u>
</b> : GAWD. Many scenes made me burst out laughing, helplessly trying to contain myself. Laurent and Damen's interactions were priceless and I'm still smiling thinking about them. The awkwardness!! GAH. It was the BEST.<br><br><b>
  <u>Perplexity</u>
</b> : I'm sorry, but I can't wrap my head around Damen's naivety. When I call something in book one, I don't expect for the MC to act all surprised when it's revealed in book <i>three</i>. I mean, how fucking stupid is he to miss the billions clues popping out everywhere? Anticlimactic at its best, sadly. <br><br><b>
  <u>Disbelief</u>
</b> : I'm not one to complain a lot about far-stretched plots in fantasy, but really, the ending did not sit well with me. Are these people for real? For all the ways that it could have ended, I found the last 20% hardly coherent and way too convenient for me to take it seriously. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>1. I already stated that <b>Damen's reaction to the fact that Laurent used to be his uncle's pet was anticlimactic</b> while it's been bloody obvious since the middle of book 1 (and I'm generous).<br><br>2. <b>Jokaste's letter is completely out of character</b> : we've been told since the start that she was a ruthless woman, clever and complex, and she would leave a <i>letter</i> stating that the child isn't Damen's? HOW FUCKING CONVENIENT. Wouldn't she want to keep this information secret to have a leverage against Damen if needed? I don't know, I might have accepted it if it hadn't been stated repeatedly that she was Laurent's equal in scheming. <br> <br>3. The <b>whole "trial" in Ios was a farce</b> in so many accounts : the multiple twists, the convenient revelation of the Regent's part in Laurent's father death... I don't know, perhaps I'm too harsh, but everything was too neat for me to buy it.<br><br>4. <b>Kastor and Laurent's fight</b> : So. Laurent has the time to bend over Damen and talk to him, <i>while Kastor doesn't make any move to get to him</i>. It seemed a little too convenient, again, to me. <br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>BUT. In the end, I'm bursting with - <br><br><b>
  <u>Pride</u>
</b> : The growth and evolution of these well-rounded characters are part of the best I ever read, with loyalty and trust in the heart of them. <b>I am so, so glad I gave these books a chance because trust me, this journey was a roller coaster of emotions, and it feels wrong to reduce it as a simple romance. This is more. So much more.</b> This said, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17158532.Kings_Rising__Captive_Prince___3_" title="Kings Rising (Captive Prince, #3) by C.S. Pacat" rel="nofollow noopener">Kings Rising</a> was notably focused on Laurent and Damen's relationship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with a twist that I had wanted to be true for so long - I LOVED the fact that he knew. PERFECT <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which wasn't the case in the two previous books. I won't say that it bothered me, given the fact that I've been waiting for some action since the beginning.<br><br>*wiggles eyebrows* <br><br>► Don't let my pang of disappointment prevent you for meeting these characters. Albeit harsh (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064714643?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of book one</a>), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4349837.C_S__Pacat" title="C.S. Pacat" rel="nofollow noopener">C.S. Pacat</a>'s story will linger in my heart a very long time. <br><br>PS. Thank you Navessa for your support through those. It was MUCH NEEDED. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3828639269104899217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425273999" href="/book/show/25810368-kings-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2224259527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7444534854158477667"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017172280' rel='nofollow noopener'>Captive Prince</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2224258844' rel='nofollow noopener'>Prince's Gambit</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 King's Rising ★★★★★</blockquote><br/><b>
  <i>Spoilers ahead for the first two books!</i>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>A kingdom, or this.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Holy hell. I was <i>not</i> ready for this series to end. What I wouldn't give for a fourth book, even if it was just full of domestic fluff and precious, tender little moments. I would pay good money for a limitless supply of Laurent's wicked snark and Damen's kindness. When I began this series, I never could have guessed that it would mean so much to me. I expected a </span>
  <span id="freeText7444534854158477667" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017172280" rel="nofollow noopener">Captive Prince</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2224258844" rel="nofollow noopener">Prince's Gambit</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 King's Rising ★★★★★</blockquote><br /><b>
  <i>Spoilers ahead for the first two books!</i>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>A kingdom, or this.</i>
</blockquote><br />Holy hell. I was <i>not</i> ready for this series to end. What I wouldn't give for a fourth book, even if it was just full of domestic fluff and precious, tender little moments. I would pay good money for a limitless supply of Laurent's wicked snark and Damen's kindness. When I began this series, I never could have guessed that it would mean so much to me. I expected a fun, dramatic romance, but I got so much more. I got politics, betrayal, war, and one of the most <i>phenomenal</i> slow burns I’ve ever seen in my life. C. S. Pacat has fully perfected the enemies-to-lovers trope, and I’m not sure that I’ll ever see it done better than it was in these books.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>There was a warmth in his chest whenever he looked at Laurent. He didn't look often for that reason.</i>
</blockquote><br />In the beginning of the book, we watch Damen and Laurent forced into yet another stand-off, and the distance is so incredibly bittersweet. My heart ached so many times in such a short span of this story, because the longing that Damen feels is described in breathtaking detail. Pacat’s capability for writing angst and turmoil shone in this final installment, but along with it, came her incredible knack for writing tenderness and care. I found myself wanting to tab entire pages, just so I could easily come back and reread them whenever I need a pick-me-up. ❤️<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I think if I gave you my heart, you would treat it tenderly.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Out of everything in this series, though, nothing took me off guard as much as the way I would grow to cherish sweet, vicious little Laurent. He is a twisted, conniving, brilliant young man, but his cleverness is unmatched and his kindnesses are so subtle and hidden that they mean all the more for it. I distinctly remember saying, while reading the first book, that I couldn’t fathom ever appreciating his character, and I was so wrong. Laurent is one of the best examples of three-dimensional writing I have ever seen, and he and Damen alike will always hold a special place in my heart for how <i>real</i> they feel.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I have not the means to defend against this.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7444534854158477667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1400304336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1400304336" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1400304336?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780698154322" href="/book/show/25372445-kings-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1400304336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4435769418827312874">One of my favourite series ever, one of the <b>most touching</b> and <b>intense love stories</b> I've ever read. It has and will always hold an exclusive place in my heart.<br/><br/><b>“Hello, lover.”</b><br/><br/>Let it be known that the <i>
  <b>Captive Prince</b>
</i> series is something beautiful, precious, heady and spectacular. I want the whole world to read this, and people, I'm going to do it. I'm going to rave about this series so much that everyone will end up reading it just to shut me up. <br/>(I won't stop even then, though.)<br/><br/>I have already s</span>
  <span id="freeText4435769418827312874" style="display:none">One of my favourite series ever, one of the <b>most touching</b> and <b>intense love stories</b> I've ever read. It has and will always hold an exclusive place in my heart.<br /><br /><b>“Hello, lover.”</b><br /><br />Let it be known that the <i>
  <b>Captive Prince</b>
</i> series is something beautiful, precious, heady and spectacular. I want the whole world to read this, and people, I'm going to do it. I'm going to rave about this series so much that everyone will end up reading it just to shut me up. <br />(I won't stop even then, though.)<br /><br />I have already specified elsewhere what it is that charms me so much about these books, but I'll repeat it, just to be sure that you can catch at least a glimpse of the impossible amount of awesomeness awaiting you among these pages.<br /><br />•Absolutely <b>perfect</b>, <b>well-rounded characters</b>. The protagonists, Laurent and Damen, are masterful literary creations, the fruits of a genius' mind. I'm not exaggerating: their conversations, their<b> interactions</b>, not only those between the two of them but also with others, are <b>precise</b>, <b>chiseled</b>, and they exactly mirror their personality so as to seem, beyond any doubt, carefully studied and thought-out, and yet their feel is incredibly <b>natural </b>and <b>spontaneous</b>. This both helps the reader to get attached to them, and provide them with a complexity that only adds to their characterization.<br /><br /><b>“Don't,” said Laurent, “toy with me. I-have not the means to-defend against this.”</b><br /><br />•Speaking of this, I've always been a fan of Pacat's <b>writing style</b>, and I'll always be. Her prose is wonderful, her sentences articulate and<b> beautifully sophisticated</b>, yet so easy to read that you find yourself swept away, but gently, in the stream of her words. <br /><br />•The <b>romance</b> (seriously, you thought I wouldn't mention that). Useless to say, it had me sold from book one, because, again, the interactions between the teo main characters are sheer perfection and each syllable that goes between them gives me thrills. The <b>excruciatingly slow</b>, and for this very reason <b>inconceivably sweet </b>and <b>gripping</b>, development of their relationship is the truest core of this story, and in my opinion it can be described only as a work of art. I know I am using a lot of hyperbolic expressions here, but, in sheer honesty, I'm usually rather reluctant to use them (and sure enough, even my four-star reviews happen to be full of reasons why to dislike the book instead of the opposite), so believe me when I say that, in these case, all my praises are totally deserved.<br />So, yes. Damen and Laurent won and broke and then mended again my poor, sore, swollen heart.<br /><br /><b>“Laurent said, “No. I’m not here to-” He said, “I'm just here.”</b><br /><br />(Yes, a lot of Laurent's quotes here. I loved him too much in this book.)<br /><br />•On the other hand, I couldn't ignore a couple of flaws (see the part where I complain about my complaining tendency). For example, I would have like to see more of that <b> twisted political intricacy</b> that we see in the second book -which is, for me, the best installment in the series. We have some here too, though, so I'm not going to mke a storm in a teacup out of this. But again, I missed seeing Laurent's sharp, cunning mind at work 24/7.<br /><br />•The <b>ending</b> is a bit rushed and <b>abrupt</b> -thank god Pacat's plans include an <a href="http://cspacat.com/announcing-the-captive-prince-adjacent-project/" rel="nofollow noopener">adjacent project</a>, which I suggest you check out. <br />Also, I had the impression that things untangled a bit too easily, and that didn't feel very realistic.<br /><br />Anyway, I can sincerely say that the book lived up to my expectations. Now the only thing that could make me happier is Pacat delivering that blessed prologue, in which, I understand, everything can happen. Hey, how am I supposed not to indulge my wildest dreams when Damen says things like this:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>“Am I such a poorer prospect than a Patran princess, or a daughter of the Empire?”</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />and the both of them say things like this:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>“We both hold the centre,” said Laurent. And then: “It was one kingdom, once.”<br />Laurent wasn't looking at him whe he said it, and it was a long moment before he lifted his eyes to Damen's waiting ones, and Damen's breath caught at what he saw there, the odd shyness of it, as though Laurent was asking instead of answering.<br />“Yes,” said Damen, feeling light headed at the question.”</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Oh my sweetness.<br /><br /><b>EDIT</b> 02/02/16: I can't believe this is happening.<br /><br /><b>EDIT </b>09/15: Please book let them be together Please book let them be together Please book let them be together Please book let them be together Please book let them be together Please book let them be together Please book let them be together.<br /><br />Did I mention they should be together?</span>
