    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_516517925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/516517925" />
    <a title="Midnight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3231173-midnight"><img alt="Midnight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266365847p2/3231173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/516517925?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Midnight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Midnight" href="/user/show/3231173-midnight">Midnight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3231173-midnight?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer516517925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15079673050651325023">After reading this final installment, I didn't feel like writing a review because I realized I had very little nice to say about it. The writing itself is great, as far as style goes and there was not a moment where I felt bored. It sure kept me at the edge of my seat, however, not in a good way. Most of the book, I've found myself frustrated, hastily reading to reach a point where my hopes would be fulfilled and I could go, "Yes! Finally justice!" Alas, that moment never came. I have to say, th</span>
  <span id="freeText15079673050651325023" style="display:none">After reading this final installment, I didn't feel like writing a review because I realized I had very little nice to say about it. The writing itself is great, as far as style goes and there was not a moment where I felt bored. It sure kept me at the edge of my seat, however, not in a good way. Most of the book, I've found myself frustrated, hastily reading to reach a point where my hopes would be fulfilled and I could go, "Yes! Finally justice!" Alas, that moment never came. I have to say, this book disappointed me on several levels, the characters, the action (some scenes), the anti-climatic ending…I've broken up my review into sections, but I will only cover the big moments, there's a lot of minor moments and things I omit, because then this would be a novel. If you loved the book, don't read further. I am aware that I'm in the minority and most people seem to love the book, but this is just my opinion and I'm not here to argue with anyone, so if you disagree, good for you but whatever.<br /><br /><b>The Regent</b><br />There's a lot to say about the Regent but for me, one of the major things that I've hated throughout the series and hoped would be shattered in this book is his Mary-Sue-esque quality. It's as though nobody can outsmart him, he is always two-five steps ahead of everyone, can predict nearly everything, keep everyone so afraid of him that nobody ever dares question him. He simply seems unstoppable and almighty, because no matter what L&amp;D do, they can't even catch up to him, nevermind keeping the pace. They never once are on equal footing with him. I find that unbelievable. It worked, to an extent, in the first two books, but in this book I expected them to finally outmaneuver him. He doesn't seem to have any weaknesses, doesn't make any true mistakes that would cost him and have dire consequences. The Council doesn't once (except in the end) question him, they believe his every word or pretend to. He was never the King, so he never should've had even half the power he attained and the fact that not even these supposedly smart council members seemed to realize it or have the guts to question it or attempt to hear Laurent's side instead of blindly believing the Regent. There was no real opposition, no attempts on his life, no rebellion or anything. There was only ever Laurent, having to fight for what is rightfully his and go it alone. Nobody truly supported, no one seemed to notice the abuse, and the rest of what the Regent did, and nobody seemed to care. The Regent is elevated to some all powerful mastermind, and even the "mistakes" (never true ones) he makes seem calculated in by him. In the end, it was some minor character's bringing him down in an almost casual "just passing through" way. Laurent and Damen, even united, never once were a real threat to him and had zero chance to defeat him.<br /><br />The whole situation with Govart is hard to believe as well. Who is Govart? Some random soldier, a nobody, what's his word worth? Nothing. Some letter written by another random and now dead soldier also means zilch. So what stopped the Regent from simply killing Govart? Nothing. Yet for some mysterious reason he not only let him live, but also gave into his demands to an extent. <br /><br /><b> Laurent</b><br />It's like Laurent becomes a whole new character in this book. He suddenly stops being smart and going with his head, and runs with his emotions and heart instead, especially at Kingsmeet. He is ready to beg and die for a guy that he's hated for years, for a guy that killed his brother and destroyed his life. And he doesn't even care about it anymore. He easily jokes around with Damen about his possible interactions with Auguste, the hatred for Damen disappears lightning fast (in this book), hell, he even easily shrugs off years of abuse and eagerly dives into bed with Damen, with no flashbacks, or flinches caused by sudden memories, no triggers or anything. It's like parts of his memory had been been wiped and he is a whole new person with no awful baggage to surface at random moments. It's like, "Oh, you'd get on with my brother like a house on fire, I'm sure. I mean, if you hadn't killed him of course. But anyhow, he'd have liked you." Ummkay. In this book, he's no longer that smart, he's not careful, he takes stupid risks (like pretending to be Charls) and makes dumb, unnecessary sacrifices, not giving a damn about all the people he managed to rally behind him. He loses sight of priorities and jeopardizes everything he's worked so hard for, for what…love? Doubtful. It just doesn't make any sense. <br /><br />Then there are the moments when his characters slides into Mary-Sue territory as well, like escaping from the cell and killing Govart, the Okton and him winning with zero explanation on how he can even do it all considering it's a foreign game he's mostly likely never tried before. <br /><br /><b>Damen</b><br />I expected Damen's character to develop and grow in this book, become stronger, not physically, but mentally. If he is supposed to rule, be the king, he needs to be less naive and be able to make tough decisions. He didn't show it here and in the baby-scene it's absolutely obvious that he is unable to do so, unable to go down to that cell and face Jokaste and tell her something like, "You know what, I don't care about some baby, there'll be others, but I need to fight for my people and kingdom here and now. Execute her." Instead he sends Laurent and then follows and listens in, like some coward. I felt like his character didn't really grow, he didn't mature or learn much from previous mistakes as evident when he offers to spare Kastor's life. In that moment, it's clear that Damen did not learn a damn thing and didn't change. He remains the ever naive fool. He doesn't even seem to clue in to the fact that Laurent's been abused, that or he doesn't care.<br /><br />Then, there is the surrender. I don't buy it for a second. Damen is consistently portrayed as a fighter, a fighter that never gives up no matter the odds. He doesn't simply surrender especially when he knows it'll likely be his death and he has little chance of saving Laurent. I mean, he had to be absolutely brainless to think he had a shot in hell with his little speech about being proud to be Laurent's lover (like that means something?). I would've expected him to get into the palace through secret passages and make a diversion, like maybe setting it on fire to create chaos and have a chance of getting Laurent out of there or alt. finally killing the Regent. But nope, he surrenders. Probably gonna surrender when he's king and there's an enemy army standing at his gates, too. I mean why not. Seems like a solid plan. For all the time the author spent building up his character as a physically strong one, a warrior, etc. it didn't matter or play any real role in the end. He stood there like a lamb facing slaughter and he couldn't even dispose of Kastor on his own. <br /><br /><b>Jokaste</b><br />In this book, Jokaste was basically transformed into Laurent 2.0 with no clear reason. It made zero sense for her to be his female copy. I tried to find a possible explanation, but there was none and thus, the transformation seemed unnecessary and highly annoying. It made Damen seem shallow, and as though he only picked Laurent because he "fit the mold" not because he actually liked him for the person he is. Jokaste's character was also completely destroyed, suddenly she became a sorts of psychic hero sacrificing herself for Damen's life. She apparently could predict everything…and then that begs the question, if she could and was as smart as we are led to believe, why couldn't she attempt to change things up by having Kastor killed off somewhere or something. No, let's take the most complicated and all around horrible path! What. Again, makes no sense. And they let her escape, along with her half-royal bastard. Wonderful.<br /><br /><b> The baby-situation</b><br />First of all, this is such a tired, old cliche and I was disappointed to see it here. There's no need for soap-opera ploys in book like this. Knowing how treacherous and conniving Jokaste is, the fact that Damen would suddenly believe that the baby was his and that he would care that much about some baby he's never seen is unbelievable. In the other books iirc it was mentioned how he probably has a ton of children running around somewhere, and he clearly didn't care about them, so why would he care about this one. It wasn't believable at all that both of them would care so much for some random baby that might not even be Damen's that they'd basically throw away everything they'd worked so hard for and alter their plans to save it. The fates of two kingdoms/nations against that of one baby...well, the choice is obvious here. <br /><br /><b>Kingsmeet</b><br />Truly one of the worst scenes in the book was the one at Kingsmeet. First of all, there is no actual reason (that'd make sense) for them to even go there. But they still risk everything to go there, meet the Regent, be utterly humiliated by him and let Laurent be captured in some mad sacrifice for Damen. It's out of character for both of them, for Laurent as a strategist he had to keep check of priorities, and he didn't. He acted like a complete fool, even when drunk he was never that stupid or careless. Damen…a fighter, his abilities showcased several times and bordering on supernatural, and he fails to use the opportunity to snap the Regent in half, really? Instead he goes raving mad attacking others and let's himself be subdued, this after he almost single-handedly won the battle in the beginning of the book? And when he thought Laurent betrayed him, on top of that? Now, with the clear threat right in front of them, and Laurent there, he should've gone for the kill, but nope. <br /><br /><b>The Council</b><br />The Council seemed absolutely useless for most of the trilogy. I wonder why they had to be painted as some mindless fools who "had one job." They never seemed to question the Regent, they never seemed to even attempt to get through to Laurent, get to know him, hear his side, etc. and looking after him and helping him was their job. They were just there, for no apparent reason, than to suddenly and miraculously switch sides in the end. It made no sense for them to suddenly turn around, either. They had to have known that Laurent was abused, unless they were completely brain dead and blind, of course. No one cared. Then suddenly they hear about Aimeric and suddenly care? There had to be at least one person, smart enough and/or brave enough to oppose the Regent earlier or at least undermine his influence yet there was nobody. Their sudden shift in views seems to make no sense and there's no real explanation either. They might as well have thrown a damn coin to help them pick sides. Considering they are the ones to "save the day" I expected more believability. <br /><br /><b>The battle with Kastor</b><br />This is another scene where any semblance of realism got thrown out the window. Damen chases after Kastor, to kill him, as one would expect considering everything that went down. But no, Damen chased after him to offer to spare his life. Believability - zero. He should've just let him get away then. After everything that Kastor's done, Damen still has trouble finishing him off? I don't believe it, not for a second. Kastor is the man that 1. Damen barely even knows, 2. Killed his father, 3. Betrayed Damen, 4. Usurped the throne and 5. Conspired with the Regent. He attacks Damen with intention to kill, and yet Damen still can't retaliate. At this point, I wondered if Damen suffered great brain damage or something. Then, along comes Laurent, to save the day and manages to dispatch Kastor despite being tied up for hours prior and despite Kastor being stronger and more experienced. Wow. Plausibility, what's that.<br /><br /><b> The Ending</b><br />After building up the characters (L&amp;D) in the first two books, showcasing their strength and intelligence to then go and end the book with them surviving thanks to sheer luck, well…If it weren't for a random happenstance, a chance of two minor character coming along and providing some poorly supported evidence and then, amazingly, the Council actually believing them, both Laurent and Damen would have been executed. I found it unbelievable for the two of them to make such great mistakes, after enduring hardships and working so hard to do away with the Regent. They hung by a very thin thread and only survived thanks to minor characters and a luck. To me, that is a ludicrous ending to this trilogy. It destroys them as characters and no amount of suspend disbelief can help it here. In this book, they are brought lower than low, humiliated on several occasion, going so far as to beg on their knees and they never get the chance to truly retaliate, there's never a chance for them to fight the Regent and defeat him. They never even get close to being on equal footing with him, nevermind winning. That was the biggest disappointment to me and made no sense. All this build up, all the sacrifices made, all the experience, all the hardships to result in such an anti-climatic end. A true shame.<br /><br />The book could've done with an Epilogue, providing a glimpse at the aftermath and tying up some loose ends. I know there's a short story coming later, but that's different. The ending of this book seemed abrupt and uncertain, leaving too many questions. What it came down to was this, "By sheer luck, the main chars escaped execution and the bad guys were quickly killed. A true miracle! End of story." After waiting for years, I expected it to be better, I expected an epic fight, a grand finale, a true victory and justice served. Therefor, I am highly disappointed with this lukewarm, anti-climatic end, where some minor whatstheirnames characters come in to save the day, while the main characters are being utter fools with zero explanation for it.<br /><br />/End of unpopular opinion. I loved the first two books, so it pains me to give this book only one star. Alas.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15079673050651325023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2490538264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2490538264" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2490538264?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2490538264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2319822261458550110"><i> “I would court you, with all the grace and courtesy that you deserve.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>For centuries wars were won this way - two countries fighting for one cause - to destroy their real enemies. <br/>War is caused by several things but the most common is the hunger for power. <br/>If you get a taste of it there is a craving, a longing that destroys your soul. <br/>It makes you ruthless, makes you lose your loyalty and makes you forget that there is something other than power - like family or love. <br/>Being betra</span>
  <span id="freeText2319822261458550110" style="display:none"><i> “I would court you, with all the grace and courtesy that you deserve.” </i> <br /><br />Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />For centuries wars were won this way - two countries fighting for one cause - to destroy their real enemies. <br />War is caused by several things but the most common is the hunger for power. <br />If you get a taste of it there is a craving, a longing that destroys your soul. <br />It makes you ruthless, makes you lose your loyalty and makes you forget that there is something other than power - like family or love. <br />Being betrayed by their own families Damen and Laurent understand that the only way to win this waris to fight together. <br />But still there are secrets that were told and hate and love that is brooding between them. But even though they don’t know if they can trust each other they are sure of one thing and one thing only - they want to take their rightful places as Kings and let justice take place. But justice is hard to gain when there is distrust between two soon-to-be-kings. <br />With every book I read in this series and with every review I write for these special books I always repeat myself: this book is full of betrayal, intrigues and lots and lots of emotions. <br />You think: How can there be any more betrayals and intrigues? Isn’t it getting boring? <br />Let me tell you one thing: this book is every other thing but certainly not boring. Definitely not boring. <br />It’s exciting and holds the reader on edge because they never know what is coming next. Who’s going to die who’s going to betray who and what will happen next? <br />I felt too many emotions and my heart was forced to take so many heartbreaks and still I’m so so satisfied and happy that I started and finished this series. <br />It wasn’t perfect, but it wasn’t awful. It was a really really good story with great characters and a nice captivating writing. <br /><br />Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />The first time I heard about this book one name was burned into my memory. <br />Laurent. <br />He was like a beautiful poisonous snake. <br />When you see it the first time it’s beautiful, fascinating and elegant and so so dangerous. <br />I was confused by my high interest in him even though I hate mean and brutal characters - but then after reading and getting to know him better I understood - behind that mask of a poisonous monster there was something deep something forced into the shadows of his character. <br />Kindness, the seeking for justice and love. <br />I was captivated by his complicated and twisted character and by his intriguing and fascinating mind. <br />I really really liked him because every time you tried to force him into a role - he broke out of it. You thought of him as a villain? <br />So he shows you contrary. <br />In this whole series he was my absolute favorite character. <br />Next to Damen of course. <br />Damen my wonderful kindhearted king. <br />He was never perfect but his character developed into something wonderfully human. <br />He sought justice and showed loyalty even though he could’ve acted differently. <br />He trusted his feelings when there was doubt and even though Laurent sometimes treated him horribly he still knew that this was the way Laurent protected himself. With words. <br />He saw behind the facade and saw the man, the real human person behind it. <br />And then he fell in love. <br />And it was wonderful. <br />I think the characters in this story are a real masterpiece. They’re twisted, complicated and you can never really place them right or predict their movements. <br />To follow their adventure was exciting and I loved every minute of it. <br /><br />Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><i> “I think if I gave your heart, you would treat it tenderly.” </i> <br />If you ever start this series be warned that there are horrible heartbreaks and other feelings you will feel. <br />Because this books won’t give you a break when you need it. It’ll destroy you only to force you back to your feet to show you something new and shocking. Something you couldn’t even predict if you tried really really hard. <br />And with forcing to go through all these heartbreaks my heart began to be vulnerable. <br />All these betrayals, intrigues and plot twist. <br />There was no time for a break - until my ship finally sailed I saw something I craved so much - happiness. Pure innocent happiness. <br />And then I wasn’t vulnerable or angry or sad anymore - I was grinning like and idiot and being a happy little reader. <br />This one is a really complicated love story where you can never be sure of anything. <br /><br />Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Even though I loved the story and the characters, I think this book has a little weakness: it’s really character driven. <br />It gave the whole story a little bit of a slow pacing. <br />I know some of you like character driven stories, but I would’ve liked a nice balance of story and characters. <br />Still it’s one of my favorite stories involving wonderful princes that love each other. <br />I’m really happy I started and finished it and maybe in a few months or years I’ll reread it in German.<br /><br /><i> “A kingdom, or this” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2319822261458550110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2111107851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2111107851" />
    <a title="Shin Mon Thway" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69053579-shin-mon-thway"><img alt="Shin Mon Thway" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504764254p2/69053579.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111107851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11112447872558098890"><b>Reread: 13th June 2018<br/><br/>Can I just say I'm simply drunk on love for these two? As amazing as ever! Seriously, the greatest trilogy of all time when it comes to MM romance. If you still haven't this one, you are seriously missing out! You know why I love rereading my favorite books? Because you always realize new things, new depths of emotions the characters develop for reach other and new perspectives. I saw more of Laurent's way of thinking and unspoken words this time I reread. He really is a so</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11112447872558098890" style="display:none"><b>Reread: 13th June 2018<br><br>Can I just say I'm simply drunk on love for these two? As amazing as ever! Seriously, the greatest trilogy of all time when it comes to MM romance. If you still haven't this one, you are seriously missing out! You know why I love rereading my favorite books? Because you always realize new things, new depths of emotions the characters develop for reach other and new perspectives. I saw more of Laurent's way of thinking and unspoken words this time I reread. He really is a softie at heart. And Damianos really is the man for him! The epitome of true love! Now I'm excited for my another reread for this trilogy! D&amp;L forever! <br><br><br><br>Original review: revised edition</b><br><br>Wow, what a journey this has been! I've finally finished "Captive prince trilogy" and I'm left filled with so many emotions. Let's start from the beginning of the book.<br><br>I love how Damiano's identity was revealed in the ending of second book and how it continued in this third book. The battle of Charcy was an epic battle scene. You can see and feel Damen's iron-clad strong will to protect Laurent. It's not a King going to war for land and glory. It's a man who would do anything to please and fulfill his lover's needs.<br><br><br><b>“To gain everything and lose everything in the space of a moment. That is the fate of all princes destined for the throne.” </b><br><br><br>What a statement! It's phenomenal and it's sooo true. I really love the reunion of Laurent and Damen after the battle of Charcy. When Laurent was hurting Damen with words, as a third person and a bystander, I can see that it hurts Laurent equally to hurt Damen. And they still decided to work together against all odds to win their thrones. They lied to themselves that they are only working together for political reasons but we all know that they can't be apart each other and they are together for their hearts' undeniable desires.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528828716i/25736546._SY540_.jpg" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love this scene when Laurent got drunk and accidentally revealed his hidden emotions to Damen. And when Damen was shocked and wrecked from the unexpected revelation from Jokaste, it was Laurent who comforted and consoled Damen against his cold and frigid nature. And the scene where they made love to each other as themselves without hiding anything, it brought me to tears, tears of happiness! It was so well written that I, myself felt like Laurent and my heart ached with emotions of forgiving Damianos with all his heart and accepting him as his one and only lover, his other part of soul. <br><br> <br><b>“When you kissed me,’ said Laurent, pushing the words out, ‘I liked it. When you took me in your mouth, it was the first time that I had . . . done that.’ He said, ‘I liked it when you—”<br><br><br>“Laurent’s reaction to kissing had always been complex: tense; vulnerable; hot.”<br><br><br>“I’m not your slave,’ said Damen. ‘I’m a man.”<br><br><br>“He couldn’t bear that suddenly. He wanted it without pretences, without excuses, his fingers curling hard into Laurent’s hair.<br>‘It’s me,’ said Damen. ‘It’s me, here with you. Say my name.’<br>‘Damianos.”<br><br><br>“the painful exchange of brother for lover, he was in some private reality where myth and man met.”<br><br><br>“Laurent said, ‘I know who you are. I know who you are. Damianos.”</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528828716i/25736547._SY540_.jpg" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528828716ra/25736548.gif" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love how Laurent changed from that moment when he finally accepted that he can't live without Damen and he has no choice but to forgive his brother's killer and accept him as his lover. It was so sooooo emotional, beautiful and heartmelting. I love how the story built up and their victory over usurpers. I love how Laurent gave himself up to the regent in order to save Damen. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528828716i/25736549._SY540_.jpg" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the ending, when I thought {author: C.S. Pacat] couldn't surprise me anymore, I'm equally surprised and very thrilled by the very last twist in the story. I love how Laurent shyly asked Damen to be forever his in the end. The ending couldn't be better. Of course, I do want more but I have no choice but to scratch my itches by reading the short stories in this series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528828716i/25736550._SX540_.jpg" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This really has been an incredible reading journey. I can see why fans from all over the world moon over D&amp;L. And the ultimate question of all D&amp;L fans comes down to me, whom I love more. Well, that's a question I'll never be able to answer. I adore both characters equally. I'm Laurent as well as Damen when I was reading this book. I really can't decide whom I love more. I'm both head over heels in love with them. I really can't thank my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4167077-al-the-serial-series-skipper" rel="nofollow noopener">Alex</a> enough for recommending me this wonderfully phenomenal series. I hope my review is helpful to those who're skeptical about whether to invest their time in these beautiful books or not.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508049862i/24178008._SY540_.jpg" width="height=" alt="description/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><br>D&amp;L will forever live in my heart!!! 😍❤️😘<br><br><br>10 It was one kingdom, once stars</b><br>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</span>
  <a data-text-id="11112447872558098890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

</b><br>BR with the darling <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40572117-saint-monique" rel="nofollow noopener">Saint Monique!</a> Thank you for being such an amazing reading buddy and for being patient with my messages that are just mostly me screaming about our babies 🙈 <b>I fully believe that this series wouldn’t be what it is for me if I didn’t have you to gush about our kingly babies with! 🧡💙🧡💙</b><br><br><b>Now, fanart of our kingly babies to bless everyone’s eyes: </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1593984611i/29767073._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Song Recommendation</i>
</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=47I2gt2J4yc" rel="nofollow noopener">Ye Tune Kya Kiya</a> with <a href="http://www.bollymeaning.com/2013/07/ye-tune-kya-kiya-lyrics-translation.html" rel="nofollow noopener">English translation</a>!<br><br><b>Saari duniyaa se jeet ke main aaya hoon idhar</b><br><i>I have won over the world and come here</i><br><b>Tere aage hi main haara, kiya tune kya asar?</b><br><i>But I’ve lost myself to you, what effect do you have on me?</i><br><b>…</b><br><b>Kyun khud ko main barbaad karron, fanna hoke tumse miloon,</b><br><i>Why should I destroy myself and meet you after being destroyed?</i><br><b>Ishq ka ajab hai kaayda</b><br><i>Love has strange rules</i><br><b>…</b><br><b>Kaho to kis se marzi loon, kaho to kis ko arzi doon</b><br><i>Tell me whose permission should I take, tell me to whom should I sent request</i><br><b>Hansta ab thoda farzi hoon, ye tune kya kiya?</b><br><i>My smiles are less fake these days, <b>what have you done to me?</b></i><br><br><b>
  <i>Review</i>
</b><br><i>Kings Rising</i> is the last full-length novel in the <b>
  <i>Captive Prince</i>
</b> trilogy, but there are two more novellas set after the events of this novel. I’m grateful for these novellas because the ending of Kings Rising was unsatisfactory and I need my kingly babies to be sickeningly sweet with each other to make up for everything they have been through in this series!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘You were never a slave, Damianos. You were born to rule, as I was.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book shows us the journey of how <b>Damen <i>’prince-killer’</i> of Akielos</b> and <b>Laurent <i>’frigid Prince’</i> of Vere</b> find their way back to each other and to their birth right as heirs after overcoming the barriers of familial betrayals, bloody battles, and, most importantly, <b>their internal struggles.</b> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘Don’t,’ he said, ‘talk about it like—’<br>‘Like?’<br>‘Like it was cold-blooded; like I controlled it. Like we didn’t both close our eyes and pretend I was a slave.’ He made himself say the exposing words. ‘I was your slave.’<br>‘There was no slave,’ said Laurent. ‘He never existed. I don’t know what manner of man stands before me now. All I know is that I am facing him for the first time.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But before I get carried away with he good parts of the book, let’s address the not so perfect parts, namely <b>the plot.</b> Dare I say it, it was anticlimactic at times. There were some subplots that were wrapped up hastily in the end of the book while others were downplayed. Specifically, there were three instances where the plot fell flat for me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>The <b>first instance</b> was when the army that Damen and Laurent had spent majority of the second book and first part of this book building and training was not used in the final showdown. I guess it spotlighted the theme that it was going to be Damen and Laurent against the opposition in their kingdom, but the time and energy they spent on building that army felt worthless. <br><br>The <b>second instance</b> was the subplot about the baby. We do find out that Damen is not the father of the baby, but he is still his uncle and it’s not reasonable or logical for the baby to not even be mentioned in the end when it was the reason for the dramatic change in the strategy on how to confront the Regent. That baby has royal blood in him and he is the heir of Akielos so it didn’t make sense to me that he wouldn’t be brought up or mentioned after the trial. I hope this gets addressed in the novellas!<br><br>Finally, <b>the third instance</b> is the anticlimactic death of the Regent. For all the vile things this pedophile has done to Laurent and countless other people, it would have made sense for Damen to be the one who gets to kill him and not some random soldier in the army. The book has been building up to the point where Regent gets defeated and killed, but the actual moment was anticlimactic since the spotlight falls on Kastor unexpectedly at the end.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Now,</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1598051813ra/29999084.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And that is my rating for the book! <br><br>As I have previously mentioned in many of my reviews and for those who have known me for a while now, it is a well known fact that romance and character development are most important elements for me in the books that I read. That’s why <b>the unconventional, complicated, yet swoon-worthy enemies to lovers romance between Damen and Laurent deserves all the stars in this galaxy.</b> The subtleness of their interactions with each other and their love made the moments between them that much more impactful. They never failed to give me feels, to have me gasping for breath, or to bring me to the edge of my seat with anticipation! <br><blockquote>
  <b><i>‘Say it,’ said Damen.<br>‘I</i> yield.<i>’ It was gritted out. Laurent’s head turned away to one side.<br>‘I want you to know,’ he said, the words thick and heavy as they pushed out of him, ‘that I could have done this any time when I was a slave.’</i></b>
</blockquote><br>Their romance was everything to me in this book and the character development for Laurent and Damen that led to the romance was undeniably strong! Damen rises to power as King of Akielos in the beginning of the book and that headstrong power and responsibility is palpable through his actions, strategic thinking, and compassion for his people. He has already shown glimpses of being a strong and good leader in previous books, but it is on a whole new level in this book! <b>Damen is majestic, dignified, and <i>kingly.</i></b> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘We are the Kings of Akielos and Vere. We will keep our state, and come to him in Ios when we ride in at the head of armies. He faces Vere and Akielos united. And he will fall to our might.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But underneath this exterior, Damen shows a side that is vulnerable, loyal to a fault, and <b>whipped</b> for his Veretian Prince. It broke my heart how strong he was for Laurent in the beginning of the book when Laurent was grappling with his feelings for Damen. It pierced my soul how Damen was patient with Laurent and always trying to mend things between them. My babies really hurt my heart and soul in the first half of the book, but it made their reunion all the more spectacular. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>This was the man who had had him whipped, the Prince of Vere, his nation’s enemy.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>While it did hurt to read Laurent’s animosity towards Damen in the first half of the book, I understood his pain and his inner turmoil. His brother, Auguste, was the only real family he had and his death gave way to more trauma in his adolescence so I understand his anger and animosity towards Damen and his uncle. <b>Laurent’s development from being the unfeeling, frigid prince of Vere to becoming more compassionate, displaying confident leadership qualities, revealing his vulnerable side to Damen, and becoming <i>kingly</i> was a heartwarming process.</b> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They were caught in each other, and when their eyes met Laurent said, ‘ Damen,’ again, like it meant everything, and as if Damen’s identity was enough, he was shuddering, pulsing against the air.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Laurent coming to terms with his feelings and accepting Damen as Damianos of Akielos paved the way for their swoon-worthy romance in the second half of the book! <b>The warmth of their relationship gave solace to my soul.</b> If the quotes are not enough to convince you of the swoon-worthiness of their romance, allow me to share with you <u>three of my <b>favorite</b> moments from this book:</u><br><br>↪ <b>This moment will FOREVER be etched in my memory and I have no words to describe the complexity and beauty of it.</b> When Damen voices a plea for Laurent to call him by his real name and to accept him for who he truly is and Laurent complies: <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b><i><br>‘I’m not your slave,’ said Damen. ‘I’m a man.’</i><br>Don’t think, <i>he’d said, because it was easier than saying,</i> Take me for who I am.<br><i>He couldn’t bear that suddenly. He wanted it without pretences, without excuses, his fingers curling hard into Laurent’s hair.<br>‘It’s me,’ said Damen. ‘It’s me, here with you. Say my name.’<br>‘Damianos.’<br>He felt the sundering in Laurent at that, the name an admission, a statement of truth that came out of him, Laurent open to him with nothing to hide behind. </i></b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>↪ <b>Moni and I have termed this moment as a wedding and the golden cuffs are wedding bands for us.</b> When Damen modified one golden cuff that he used to wear while he was Laurent’s pet for Laurent to wear as a show of their camaraderie since it matches the other golden cuff that Damen still wears: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i><br>The squire drew back the cloth to reveal a gold cuff. He felt rather than saw the tightness in Laurent. The cuff, unmistakably, was the twin to the one Damen wore, altered last night by a blacksmith for Laurent’s finer wrist.<br>Damen said, ‘Wear it for me.’<br>For a moment he thought Laurent wasn’t going to do it. But in public, Laurent had no recourse to refusal.<br>Laurent extended his hand. And then waited, palm outstretched, his eyes lifting to meet Damen’s.<br>Laurent said, ‘Put it on me.’<br>…<br>‘I’m overjoyed to wear a gift that reminds me of you,’ said Laurent. The cuff locked into place. He didn’t withdraw his wrist, just left it leaned on the arm of the throne, laces open and gold cuff in full view. </i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>↪ <b>Moni and I are referring to this moment as a marriage proposal.</b> When Damen asks Laurent if they can rule their lands together: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i><br>‘I hated you,’ said Laurent. ‘I hated you so badly I thought I’d choke on it. If my uncle hadn’t stopped me, I would have killed you. And then you saved my life, and every time I needed you, you were there, and I hated you for that, too.’<br>…<br>‘Is there no way forward for us?’ said Damen. It just came out. Beside him, he could feel Laurent holding himself very still. <br>‘You mean, will I come back to your bed for the little time we have left?’<br>‘I mean that we hold the centre. We hold everything from Acquitart to Sicyon. Can we not call it a kingdom and rule it together? Am I such a poorer prospect than a Patran princess, or a daughter of the Empire?’ </i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>There are so many more moments and quotes that I would like to share so if you would like to fangirl or gush about this series and these characters, my inbox is forever open!</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Final Thoughts</i>
</b><br>First, let me grace my review with the kingly presence of my favorite two kingly kings (have I mentioned how kingly they are? 🙈)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597084452i/29945529._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you think that they are overdressed in this fanart, I have a steamy surprise for you in the spoiler tag at the end 😉<br><br><u>Now, let’s wrap up this gush fest!</u><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>It was over; like a balance restored, the past put to rest.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, all I have to say is that Laurent and Damen own my body, mind, and soul. I breathe for them, I exist for them, and <b>I live for them.</b> Back in April 2020, if you would have told me I would get this attached to characters where I basically interweave them in every bookish conversation I have, then I would have laughed at your face and called you crazy. But now I’m the crazy one because I am unashamedly obsessed with rare few characters including Damen and Laurent. <br><br>If you are not fazed by the trigger warnings that accompany the first book and if you have not read this series already, I don’t know what you are waiting for. <b>Consider this an official order from me and go read the damn series. </b> And then come back and spam my inbox so I can gush about this series and characters some more with you! <br><br>Speaking of reading this series, <b>HUGE</b> shoutout to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58714144-tears-of-venus-but-humans-call-me-mina" rel="nofollow noopener">Mina</a>, for letting me vent and gush about these characters and loving these kingly babies vicariously through me! I can’t wait when you actually dive in to read these books. Be prepared for my screaming in your comments 🖤<br><br>Finally, here is the promised fanart!<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1598051813i/29999085.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><blockquote>💙🧡💙🧡💙🧡💙🧡💙🧡</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1534387930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1534387930" />
    <a title="LenaLena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4033763-lenalena"><img alt="LenaLena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362798973p2/4033763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1534387930?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LenaLena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LenaLena" href="/user/show/4033763-lenalena">LenaLena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25792894-kings-rising">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033763-lenalena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033763-lenalena?shelf=mm">mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1534387930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14256435297774410711">The first third of this book was 5 stars. Laurent and Damen as we've come to know and love them. Laurent with his mind like a nest of scorpions, juxtaposed by straightforward and honorable Damen, who can read him so well. It's dramatic, it's complicated and it's heart warming, this first third. In the second third the niggles of doubt started to set in. I honestly don't mind suspending disbelieve in a romantic fantasy novel, but it was starting to get strained. Both men are crowding into superhe</span>
  <span id="freeText14256435297774410711" style="display:none">The first third of this book was 5 stars. Laurent and Damen as we've come to know and love them. Laurent with his mind like a nest of scorpions, juxtaposed by straightforward and honorable Damen, who can read him so well. It's dramatic, it's complicated and it's heart warming, this first third. In the second third the niggles of doubt started to set in. I honestly don't mind suspending disbelieve in a romantic fantasy novel, but it was starting to get strained. Both men are crowding into superhero territory and -beyond a certain rah!rah! appeal- I didn't like that it started to eat away at the complexity of the story that was being told.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Laurent picking up a heavy oak chair with his stabbed AND dislocated arm and swinging it hard enough to kill Govart? Doubtful. Laurent excelling at the Okton, just after Damen has extensively mused how good riding and good spear throwing aren't enough for this discipline, how he himself has had to train for years? Convenient for moving the plot forward, but highly unlikely. Damen grabbing a spear coming for him out mid air? Please. Is this even necessary? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It is the last third of the book where I could not help but be disappointed. It seemed to me that by insisting on a conventional romance novel ending, crimes were committed against the characterization of both the MCs and the supporting cast, against the wonderful complexity of the plot and to the series setup as a whole. All of a sudden Laurent becomes dumb, Damen becomes oblivious, the Regent incapable and Kastor, who was never really in the books in the first place, could have been replaced by a card board cutout when he first lays eyes on his brother again after his betrayal. I had expected much more deviousness from Jokaste too, after all, she had been described as the female equivalent of Laurent. The reader is presented with a lot of hand-wavy solutions, that lean way too heavy on luck and coincidence, and that just don't hold up to any scrutiny.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For instance, the reader <s>knows</s> strongly suspects since book 1 that the Regent has used Laurent as a pet when he was a child. There are several more heavy handed clues in this book. Damen, who is an expert in reading Laurent (even when he is trying to hide his thoughts) somehow misses <i>all</i> of them. Then Laurent, (in what is a wtf setup in the first place) for unclear reasons, fails to realize that, or course, his Uncle will use this piece of information against him and Damen. He not only fails to plan for that contingency, he also fails to prepare Damen for it. Sure, he'd prefer Damen not to have put 2+2 together, but Laurent has proven over and over again he will do anything, and suffer anything, to gain advantage. In fact, I can even see him use a line like ' The only people I've fucked are my uncle and my brother's killer.' if it could get him something that he wanted badly enough. The series of events that follows after this scene is unlikely, illogical and far fetched. The whole trial is odd, with people changing sides for flimsy reasons and on hear say, the Regent suffering from his own sudden a-typical lack of contingency planning and the aforementioned card board cutout Kastor. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The only reason for this deviation from the style of the former 2.5 books that I can come with is that Laurent needed to be molded into a more conventional romance novel type hero(ine?) willing to self sacrifice for Lurve. In the process, his cunning and abrasiveness get dialed down from 'ruthless' to 'quirky'. Personally, I found that a bit insulting to his character. I would have much preferred more battles (which I am normally not a fan of) and tactical planning and double dealing than this simplistic scheme with the fluffy outcome.<br /><br />Still worth reading, but volume 2 remains by far the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14256435297774410711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_670043155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670043155" />
    <a title="Trisha Harrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10383101-trisha-harrington"><img alt="Trisha Harrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492537051p2/10383101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670043155?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha Harrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha Harrington" href="/user/show/10383101-trisha-harrington">Trisha Harrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<div id="review_2100695118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100695118" />
    <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog"><img alt="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484605631p2/44673856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100695118?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog">Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100695118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18390435085192357761"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477939914i/21011921.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>➦I've been meaning to read this trilogy for a long time and now, finally, I've read all three books back to back. This will be a quick review of the trilogy as a whole.<br/><br/>➦My overall impression was positive. But I was surprised by a couple of things. I've expected this fantasy to have, well, more fantasy?<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503429277ra/23662868.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>➦This felt a bit like... like... Game of Thrones pumped full of testosterone and minus the dragons. Or magic. Ok, forget it, it wasn't like GoT. But there was a battle for the throne (or two) and i</span>
  <span id="freeText18390435085192357761" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477939914i/21011921.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➦I've been meaning to read this trilogy for a long time and now, finally, I've read all three books back to back. This will be a quick review of the trilogy as a whole.<br><br>➦My overall impression was positive. But I was surprised by a couple of things. I've expected this fantasy to have, well, more fantasy?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503429277ra/23662868.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➦This felt a bit like... like... Game of Thrones pumped full of testosterone and minus the dragons. Or magic. Ok, forget it, it wasn't like GoT. But there was a battle for the throne (or two) and it felt like most characters were those of the male variety. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503429278ra/23662869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➦D'uh, exactly. It's an M/M novel. But still? Anyways. A captive prince sold to slavery to another prince. Sounds fun! A lot of action, twists and betrayals in this trilogy to keep a reader interested until the end, but no magic. It's a fantasy world with lots of fighting but a traditional kind, with swords and such. Yeah, not even a little bit of magic. It's ok, I got over it. It was still good.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503429278ra/23662870.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➦Another surprise was how slow burn this was. Also, not a bad thing. But if you're expecting pokepoke you might not get it for a while. May be some strokestroke to keep you interested. lol I know, so eloquently put.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503429278ra/23662871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➦Ok, so, to sum it up: if you're looking for M/M fantasy with a lot of war strategizing, action and twists then this is for you! And in the midst of it all is a slow burn romance between two people who are very unlikely to ever trust each other or be friends. But no magic.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488327168ra/22102203.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118337i/22283577.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.instagram.com/steamyreads/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118337i/22283578.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on instagram" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://steamyreads.net/youtube/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490120705i/22283756.png" width="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://www.steamyreads.net" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118159i/22283551._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XDYgR1dxpw5UG3a1YkuvFJPjm4k7iRngsi9j5qCKi7vDM4Fq3SP/E0aRwEGzzQHaK+/VKyd8U6CRxBOtwCVuiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JAZhZt7w/Q/b5xzFNRa4SU4p1QNMjltlrjxvA/WSpVG7A8BLVKKlEsltqjHkkBaH9iWboVB7ESWN1x9IlT1AYw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3071193040377084676">C.S. Pacat is a Melbourne writer. Her first series the <i>Captive Prince</i> trilogy began its life as an original web serial. Self-published in 2013 to critical and commercial success and acclaim, the <i>Captive Prince</i> trilogy was acquired by Penguin, and will be published worldwide in 2015.<br/></span>
